Jamison Brereton

84
Indra
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
20 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ6, uс╣гс╣Зih 7тАУ9, paс╣Еkti 10тАУ12, g─Бyatr─л 13тАУ15, triс╣гс╣нubh 16тАУ18, br╠еhat─л 19, satobr╠еhat─л 20; arranged in tr╠еcas 1тАУ18, prag─Бtha 19тАУ20
Coming at the end of GotamaтАЩs Indra collection, this long and metrically com plex hymn must actually be composed of smaller hymn segments. The first eighteen verses are arranged in tr╠еcas, and it ends with a single prag─Бtha. The contents range from the most banal invitation to the sacrifice to elusive and allusive treatments of little-known myths. There are a number of reminiscences of the Indra hymns pre ceding it in the Gotama collection.
The first six verses, in anuс╣гс╣нubh meter, appear to form a unity, urging Indra to come to the soma sacrifice in clich├йd and predictable phraseology. The next tr╠еca (vss. 7тАУ9) is in uс╣гс╣Зih meter (8 8 12); the last four syllables of the third p─Бda are a semidetached refrain (тАЬIndra indeed!тАЭ), so that the verses present themselves like g─Бyatr─л (i.e., 8 8 8). The contrast between the good sacrificer and his unsatisfactory counterpart is the theme.
The next tr╠еca (vss. 10тАУ12), in paс╣Еkti meter, is highly reminiscent of I.80, also in paс╣Еkti. As in that hymn the fifth p─Бda of each verse is a refrain syntactically unconnected to the rest of the verse. In fact, the last six syllables of the refrain match those of I.80, and in order to make sense of the refrain here, we must supply the verb (тАЬthey cheer onтАЭ) from the refrain of I.80. This tr╠еca concerns the mix
ing of milk with the pressed soma, in metaphorical termsтАФwith the milk streams depicted as buffalo-cows. Beneath this first metaphor there may be a second: it is possible that the Maruts lurk behind the buffalo-cow facade. (Remember that the Maruts were one of the possible subjects of the refrain in I.80.) An association of the Maruts with тАЬthe ritual midpointтАЭ here might allude to their recent incorpora
tion as recipients of the oblation at the Midday Pressing.
Another reminiscence of I.80 is found in the next tr╠еca (vss. 13тАУ15), in g─Бyatr─л, which treats in most condensed and puzzling fashion the myth of Dadhya├▒c and the horseтАЩs head. (For this myth in general, see Macdonell 1897: 141тАУ42.) Dadhya├▒c and his father Atharvan were mentioned in passing in the last verse of I.80 (vs. 16). In other versions of the myth Dadhya├▒c substitutes a horseтАЩs head for his own in order to declare the secret location of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs soma. In these three short verses we find Dadhya├▒c, the horseтАЩs head, and Tvaс╣гс╣нar, but the narrative in which they are involved is entirely unclear and we confess ourselves mystified.
The last tr╠еca (vss. 16тАУ18) consists entirely of anxious questions, mostly in con nection with the sacrifice, reminiscent of the cascade of questions in other Gotama hymns (I.75.3, 76.1, 77.1). The first verse (16) wonders who will be able to yoke particularly ill-behaved cattle and bring them here. тАЬHereтАЭ seems to refer to the sacrifice, and the best guess as to the identity of the cattle is the Maruts, who are the dedicands of GotamaтАЩs next four hymns (I.85тАУ88). The next verse (17) is more confused, but the location of Indra and indeed his very existence are in question, and a formal spokesman on behalf of mortals is sought. The questions are more clearly ritual in verse 18, ending with the sacrificerтАЩs self-doubt about his status with the gods he sacrifices to. The final two verses (19тАУ20), an independent prag─Бtha, seem designed to quell this doubt, asserting that Indra himself, in a turn-about, will praise the sacrificer and show him mercy, as well as offering him help and goods.
Although no strong unity among the various pieces of this hymn is perceptible, it does mimic in certain ways the progress of a soma sacrifice. It opens with the invita tion (vss. 1тАУ6), made more pointed by the contrast between our well-made and deserv ing sacrifice and the behavior of ungenerous mortals (vss. 7тАУ9). Verses 10тАУ12 concern the actual preparation of the soma (and also refer, in vs. 7, to the ritual midpoint). Verses 13тАУ15 can be seen as a mythic interlude, praising the great deeds of Indra while he is present on the ritual ground. Verses 16тАУ18 raise doubts about the efficacy of the sacrifice that has been, or is being, performedтАФdoubts somewhat allayed by the final two verses (19тАУ20), which end with the usual requests for benefits from the god.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рджрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЛрд╜рднреВрддреН ред рд╣реЗ рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреН рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреЛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрд░реНрд╖рдпрд┐рддрд░рд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЖ рдЧрд╣рд┐ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирджреЗрд╢рдорд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ ред рдЖрдЧрддрдВ рдЪ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдиреЗрдиреЛрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрдореН рдЖ рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ рдЖрдкреВрд░рдпрддреБ ред рд░рдЬрдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреИрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рди ред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рдкреВрд░рдпрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда ред рд╢рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдЮреНрд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдирд┐ тАШ рд╡рд┐рдиреНрдорддреЛрд░реНрд▓реБрдХреН’ред’ рдЯреЗрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЯрд┐рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рдкрд╛рджрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЧрд╣рд┐ ред рдЧрдореЗрд░реНрд▓реЛрдЯрд┐: рдмрд╣рд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред’ рдЕрдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп тАШрдЕрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╡рджрддреНрд░рд╛ рднрд╛рддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╣реЗрдГ рд▓реБрдЧрднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда рдмрд▓рд╡рддреНрддрдо ред рд╢рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рдЪреН-рдЫрдмреНрджрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрдардирд┐ ‘рд╡рд┐рдиреНрдорддреЛрд░реНрд▓реБрдХреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреБрдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН, ‘рдЯреЗрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЯрд┐рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рд╣реЗ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреЛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрд░реНрд╖рдпрд┐рддрдГ ред ‘рддреНрд░рд╕рд┐рдЧреГрдзрд┐рдзреГрд╖рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреЗрдГ рдХреНрдиреБрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрдиреБрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдЖрдЧрд╣рд┐ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреНрдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН ред рдЧрдореЗрд╢реНрд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред

рдХрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрд╡рдореБрдЪреНрдпрд╕ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН? рддреНрд╡рджрд░реНрдердореН рдЕрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдореЛрд╜рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реН - рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддрд┐ ред

рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ - рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдиреЗрди рдЪ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрддрд╛рдВ рдЧрддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЖрдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ рдЖрдкреВрд░рдпрддреБ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдорд┐рд╡ рд░рдЬ рдЙрджрдХрдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рднреВрддреИрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдкреВрд░рдпрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma has been expressed, Indra, for you; potent humber (of your foes), approach; may vigour fill you (by Soma), as the sun fills the firmament with his rays.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The soma has been pressed for you, Indra. O strongest bold one, come here.
Let Indrian strength permeate you, as the sun permeates the airy realm with its rays.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unlike the standard tr., Witzel Got┼Н take r├бjaс╕е тАШRaumтАЩ with the frame, not the simile: тАЬтАж soll dich (und) den Raum erf├╝llen, wie die Sonne тАжтАЭ I assume this is because the simile particle n├б, which usually follows the first word of a simile, here follows the second word, by most interpretations (r├бjaс╕е s┼л╠Бryo n├б ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е). This does not seem to me sufficient reason to split apart this cosmological image. I attribute the position of n├б to the particularly close association of s┼л╠Бrya- and ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е, which are frequently adjacent (cf. esp. the identical simile but without a third term тАж s┼л╠Бryo n├б ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е in VIII.43.32, IX.41.5).

Griffith

The Soma hath been pressed for thee, O Indra; mightiest, bold One, come.
May Indra-vigour fill thee full, as the Sun fills mid-air with rays.

Keith

The Soma hath been pressed for thee O Indra;
O most strong, O impetuous one, come hither;
Let power encompass thee,
Even as the sun encompasses the atmosphere with its rays.

Grassmann

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛, рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдФрд░ рдкрд╛рдард╢рд╛рд▓рд╛рдУрдВ рдХреА рд╕рднрд╛рдУ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛, рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдФрд░ рдкрд╛рдард╢рд╛рд▓рд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╕рднреНрдпрдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреА рднреА рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреЛ рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рдпрдГ рд╕реЛрдореЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐ рдпрд╕реНрддреЗ рддрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднреА рд░рдЬреЛ рдиреЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпреЗрддреН рддрдВ рддреНрд╡рдорд╛рдЧрд╣рд┐ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ рд╕ рдЪ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдорд╛рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ рее рез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддреНрдпрдореБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐) рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджреНрдпрддреЗ (рд╕реЛрдордГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдореЛрд╜рдиреЗрдХрд╡рд┐рдзрд░реЛрдЧрдирд╛рд╢рдХ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рд░рд╕рдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд╣реЗрддреЛ (рддреЗ) рддреБрднреНрдпрдореН (рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда) рдмрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрда (рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреЛ) рдкреНрд░рдЧрд▓реНрдн (рдЖ) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗ (рдЧрд╣рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдкреГрдгрдХреНрддреБ) рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдХрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдореН) рдордирдГ (рд░рдЬрдГ) рд▓реЛрдХрд╕рдореВрд╣рдореН (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ) рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рдХрд┐рд░рдгреИрдГ рее рез рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay his horses bear Indra, who is of irresistible prowess, to the praises and sacrifices of sages and of men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two fallow bays convey Indra of irresistible strength
up to the praises of the seers and to the sacrifice of the sons of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the chiasmic structure of cd: [с╣Ы╠Бс╣г─лс╣З─Бс╣Г (GEN.) ca stut─л╠Бс╕е (ACC.)] ├║pa [yaj├▒├бс╣Г (ACC.) ca m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─Бn─Бm (GEN.)]. This could have been sketched in tr. by тАЬup to the seersтАЩ praises and the sacrifice of the sons of Manu.тАЭ

Griffith

His pair of Tawny Coursers bring Indra of unresisted might
Hither to Rsis’ songs of praise and sacrifice performed by men.

Keith

Indra his two steeds bear,
Him of unequalled strength,
To the praises of the Rsis and the sacrifice of men.

Geldner

Den Indra, gegen dessen St├дrke nicht anzukommen ist, fahren die beiden Falben her zu den Lobliedern der Rishi┬┤s und zum Opfer der Menschenkinder.

Grassmann

English translation:

тАЬSlayer of Vс╣Ыtra, ascend your chariot, for your horses have been yoked by prayer; may the stone (that bruises the Soma) attract, by its sound, your mind towards us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Mount the chariot, Vr╠еtra-smasher: your two fallow bays have been yoked with a sacred formulation.
Let the pressing stone with its call make your mind inclined hither.

Griffith

Slayer of Vrtra, mount thy car; thy Bay Steeds have been yoked by prayer.
May, with its voice, the pressing-stone draw thine attention hitherward.

Keith

Mount thy car, O slayer of Vrtra;
Thy steeds are yoked by our prayer;
May the pressing-stone with its voice
Incline thy mind towards us.

English translation:

тАЬOffer worship quickly to Indra; recite hymns (in his praise); let the effused drops exhilarate him; pay adoration to his superior strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Chant now to Indra and speak solemn words.
The pressed drops have exhilarated him. Do homage to (his)
preeminent might.

Griffith

Sing glory now to Indra, say to him your solemn eulogies.
The drops poured forth have made him glad: pay reverence to his might supreme.

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Indra, you harness your horses, there is no one a better charioteer than you; no one is equal to you in strength; no one, although well-horsed, has overtaken you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

No one is a better charioteer than you, Indra, when you control your two fallow bays.
No one has reached you in greatness, not (even) one with good horses.

Griffith

When, Indra, thou dost yoke thy Steeds, there is no better charioteer:
None hath surpassed thee in thy might, none with good steeds o’ertaken thee.

Geldner

Keiner ist ein besserer Wagenlenker, wenn du, Indra, die Falben z├╝gelst. Keiner hat es dir an Macht gleichgetan, kein Rosset├╝chtiger.

Grassmann

Kein bessrer Lenker ist als du, wenn Indra du die F├╝chse lenkst, An Gr├╢sse kommt dir keiner gleich, kein schneller Reiter holt dich ein.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHe who alone bestows wealth upon the man who offers him oblations, is the undisputed sovereign, Indra–ho!тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This hymn and the two following hymns end with the term, aс╣Еga, quick; it is, perhaps, an interjection of calling: ho!

Jamison Brereton

He who alone apportions the goods to the pious mortal,
the unrepulsable master тАУ (thatтАЩs) Indra indeed!

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take ├нndro aс╣Еg├б as the main clause corresponding to the rel. cl. introduced by y├бс╕е.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions, ad I.7.8) suggests that each of these three verses reads like a brahmodya, with the last two words (the four-syllable tag ├нndro aс╣Еg├б, which he considers to be prose тАЬquite out of the metreтАЭ) serving as the answer. This analysis words best for vs. 7, but his separation of the two-word tag from the rest of the verse is clearly correct for all three verses – though I do not think we need to consider ├нndro aс╣Еg├б тАЬsimple prose.тАЭ

Griffith

He who alone bestoweth on mortal man who offereth gifts,
The ruler of resistless power, is Indra, sure.

Geldner

Der ganz allein dem opferspendenden Sterblichen Gut austeilt, der unbehinderte Gebieter ist einzig Indra:

Grassmann

Der einzig reiches Gut ertheilt dem Sterblichen, der ihn verehrt, Der Herr, dem niemand widersteht, nur Indra ist’s.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen all he trample with his foot upon the man who offers no oblations, as if upon a coiled-up snake; when will Indra listen to our praises? ho!тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Coiled-up snake: kс╣гumpa is explained as: ahicchatraka, a thorny plural nt which is taken to conjure up a snake coiled up, or one sleeping in a ring and hence, killed easily: maс╣Зс╕Нalakareс╣Зa ┼Ыay─Бnam ka┼Ыcidan─Бyasena hanti

Jamison Brereton

When will he kick the ungenerous mortal with his foot like a mushroom? When will he listen to our hymns? тАУ Indra indeed!

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax kс╣г├║mpa- is universally rendered by modern tr. as тАШmushroomтАЩ, though there is no unanimity in earlier interpretations (cf., e.g., Grassmann: Staude [perennial plant]). There is some etymological support for тАШmushroomтАЩ from modern languages (see EWA s.v.), and тАШmushroomтАЩ works well in the simile, since kicking many varieties of mushroom demolishes them, whereas a perennial plant is generally a sturdier entity. I might go so far as to suggest specifically a puffball, since kicking puffballs releases a satisfying cloud of dust (easily viewed on various YouTube videos), and puffballs do appear to be found in the appropriate geographical area.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions, ad I.7.8) suggests that each of these three verses reads like a brahmodya, with the last two words (the four-syllable tag ├нndro aс╣Еg├б, which he considers to be prose тАЬquite out of the metreтАЭ) serving as the answer. This analysis words best for vs. 7, but his separation of the two-word tag from the rest of the verse is clearly correct for all three verses – though I do not think we need to consider ├нndro aс╣Еg├б тАЬsimple prose.тАЭ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдиреНрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ ! рднрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкрджрд╛ рдХреНрд╖реБрдореНрдкрдорд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдзрд╕рдВ рдорд░реНрддреНрддрдВ рдХрджрд╛ рд╕реНрдлреБрд░рддреН рдХрджрд╛ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдкрджрд╛ рдХреНрд╖реБрдореНрдкрдорд┐рд╡ рд╕реНрдлреБрд░рддреН рдХрджрд╛ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдЧрд┐рд░рдГ рд╢реБрд╢реНрд░рд╡рджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рдпрдорд╛рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрдорд╣реЗ рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

English translation:

тАЬIndra, grant formidable strength to him who worships him, having libations prepared–ho!тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For someone who has pressed soma seeks to entice you here, away from the many.
He has control of powerful strength тАУ Indra indeed!

Jamison Brereton Notes

A broken construction. The subject of the 3rd ps. verb in c (patyate) must be Indra, though he is represented by 2nd ps. tv─Б in the apparent rel. cl. of ab. (The parallel in III.36.4b ugr├бс╣Г ┼Ы├бvaс╕е patyate dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зv ├│jaс╕е, where Indra is undeniably the subject, makes it clear that the mortal soma-presser of our ab cannot be the subject of patyate.) The y├б- clause of ab thus has no direct grammatical connection with what ought to be its main clause in c, and I therefore take y├б┼Ы cid as the functional equivalent of the indefinite k├б┼Ы cid.

I.84.10-12: See published introduction. for the structure of this tс╣Ыca and its relation to I.80. The subjects of all three verses are feminine (gaury├ас╕е, y─Б╠Бс╕е тАж say─Б╠Бvar─лс╕е 10; t─Б╠Б(с╕е) тАж pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е, тАж dhen├бvaс╕е 11; t─Б╠Б(с╕е) 12; v├бsv─лс╕е 10-12), but, in my opinion, the hidden referent of all three verses is the Maruts. See also comm. on vs. 16.

07-09 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions, ad I.7.8) suggests that each of these three verses reads like a brahmodya, with the last two words (the four-syllable tag ├нndro aс╣Еg├б, which he considers to be prose тАЬquite out of the metreтАЭ) serving as the answer. This analysis words best for vs. 7, but his separation of the two-word tag from the rest of the verse is clearly correct for all three verses – though I do not think we need to consider ├нndro aс╣Еg├б тАЬsimple prose.тАЭ

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe white cows drink of the sweet Soma thus poured forth, and associated with the bountiful Indra, for the sake of beauty, rejoice; abiding (in their stalls), they are expectant of his sovereignty.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This hymn and the following two hymns end with the refrain: vasv─лranu svar─Бjyam, lit. dwelling after, according to, his own dominion. ‘These cows who, by giving milk, are the means of providing habitaiton (niv─Бsak─Бriс╣Зyaс╕е), remain looking to the kingdom of him, or Indra’

Jamison Brereton

The buffalo-cows drink just so of the sweet honey belonging to the (ritual) midpoint,
they who, fellow travelers with bullish Indra, become exhilarated for beautyтАФ
тАУ The good ones (cheer) on his sovereignty.214 I.85

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (followed by Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) takes the feminine plurals as referring to the milk streams, mixing with the soma, here called honey. This of course accords well with the feminine gender, and I agree that this is the first layer of reference. But both the refrain, echoing the refrain of I.80, which has the Maruts as one set of subjects, and say─Б╠Бvar─лс╕е тАШfellow travellers, driving along withтАЩ point to the Maruts as a second layer.

The adj. say─Б╠Бvan- is used 3x (out of 6) with the instr. pl. of dev├б-, once (X.113.2) quite clearly of the Maruts along with Indra. Why would the hyper-masculine Maruts be referred to with feminines? I think the point is to conflate two of the sources of IndraтАЩs mastery: the soma-milk mixture animatized as cows, which enhances his physical strength, and the Maruts, who provide verbal encouragement and moral support.

I construe instr. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣З─Б with say─Б╠Бvar─лс╕е rather than with m├бdanti as most tr. do.

The latter is of course possible.

Griffith

The juice of Soma thus diffused, sweet to the taste, the bright cows drink,
Who for the sake of splendour close to mighty Indra’s side rejoice, good in their own supremacy.

Geldner

Die Gaurik├╝he trinken von dem s├╝├Яen Met, der daselbst der Mittelpunkt ist, die sich mit dem Bullen Indra als seine Begleiter erg├╢tzen, um stattlich anzusehen. Die Guten jubeln seiner Selbstherrlichkeit zu.

Grassmann

Die K├╝he trinken von dem Meth, dem s├╝ssen, welcher ringsum str├╢mt, Sie, die dem Indra zugesellt, zur Lust sich letzen an dem Stier, lichthell in eigner Herrlichkeit.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDesirous of his contact, those bridled cows dilute the Soma with their milk; the kine that are loved of Indra direct his destructive thunderbolt against his foes, abiding (in their stalls) expectant of his sovereignty.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These dappled ones, eager for caresses, prepare the soma for him. The milk-cows dear to Indra propel his mace, his missile.
тАУ The good ones (cheer) on his sovereignty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse contains another clue that the Maruts are the underlying referent.

The fem. subjects are identified as pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е тАШdappledтАЩ, but pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыni- is also the name of the MarutsтАЩ mother. They would be called Pс╣Ы┼Ыnis here, just as they are regularly called Rudras, after their father Rudra. Note the phonetic figure pr╠е┼Ыan─Бy├║vaс╕е … pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е.

Griffith

Craving his touch the dappled kine mingle the Soma with their milk.
The milch-kine dear to Indra send forth his death-dealing thunderbolt, good in their own supremacy.

Geldner

Nach ihm liebesbr├╝nstig mischen die scheckigen K├╝he den Soma; die lieben Milchk├╝he des Indra spornen die Keule, sein Wurfgescho├Я an. Die Guten jubeln seiner Selbstherrlichkeit zu.

Grassmann

Die Schecken schmiegen l├╝stern sich an ihn, dem Soma beigemischt, Die K├╝he, die dem Indra lieb, bef├╢rdern ihm sein Blitzgeschoss, lichthell in eigner Herrlichkeit.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThese intelligent kine reverence his prowess with the adoration (of their milk); they celebrate his manly exploits as an example to later (adversaries); abiding (in their stalls), expectant of his sovereignty.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They, forethoughtful, serve his might with reverence.
They follow his many commandments, to be first in his thought.
тАУ The good ones (cheer) on his sovereignty.

Griffith

With veneration, passing wise, honouring his victorious might,
They follow close his many laws to win them due preeminence, good in their
own supremacy.

Geldner

Sie huldigen ehrf├╝rchtig seiner Macht, die Klugen; sie befolgen seine vielen Gebote, um seine erste Sorge zu sein. Die Guten jubeln seiner Selbstherrlichkeit zu.

Grassmann

Sie ehren seine Siegerkraft anbetend voller Achtsamkeit, Sie folgen seinen Satzungen, den mannichfachen auf den Wink, lichthell in eigner Herrlichkeit.

Elizarenkova

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

рджрдзреНрдпрдЩреНрдирд╛рдорд░реНрд╖рд┐рд░рд╛рдерд░реНрд╡рдгрдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдерднрд┐рдГ ‘рдЕрд╕реНрдерд┐рджрдзрд┐рд╕рдХреНрдереНрдпрдХреНрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдВ"рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдкрд┐рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ’рдЗрддреНрдпрдирдЩреН ред рддрдиреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддреЗрди рд╡рдЬреЗрдг рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╡рд╛рд░рдХрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рдЬрдШрд╛рди рд╣рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдХреБрддрдГ рдХреЗрдирдЪрд┐рджрдкреНрдпрдирднрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ ред рд╕реНрдХреБрдЮреН рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╡рдгреЗ ред рдХреЗрди рдЪрд┐рджрдкреНрдпрдирднрд┐рднреВрддрдГ ред

рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ - рдЕрдкреНрддрддрд┐рд╖реНрдХреБрддрдГ рдЕрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд░рдердГ ред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХреВрд▓рдорд╛рдЪрд░рдиреНрддреЛ рдпрдВ рдХреБрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рджрдиреНрддреЛрд╜рднрд┐рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдХреБрддрдГ ред рдкреГрд╖реЛрджрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдГ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд┐рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ - рдирд╡рддреАрд░реНрдирд╡ рджрд╢рд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯреМ рдЪ рд╢рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдмрд╣реБрддрдорд╛рдиреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕ рдПрд╡рдорд┐рдорд╛рдореБрдкрджрдзрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, with the bones of Dadh─лci, slew ninety times nine Vс╣Ыtras.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dadhya├▒c = Dadh─лca and Dadh─лci, a sage. His bones formed the thunderbolt of Indra. dadhya├▒c, son of Atharvan, like the asuras, was intimidated and tranquilized by his appearance; but, when he went to svarga, the asuras overspread the whole earth. Indra, inquiring what had become of him and if something of him was left behind, was told that the horse’s head with which he had at one time taught the madhuvidy─Б to the a┼Ыvins, was somewhere in existence, but no one knew where. After a searth, it was found in the lake ┼Ъaryaс╣З─Бvat, near Kurukс╣гetra. With the bones of the skull, Indra slew the asuras (i.e. foiled the nine times ninety or eight hundred and ten, strategems or devices of the asuras or Vс╣Ыtras]. The number is accounted for by the legend that in the beginning, the ─Бsur─л m─Бy─Б (demoniac illusion) was practised in the three worlds, for three periods (past, present, and future), thus becoming nine-fold; each was exerted with three ┼Ыaktis or energies, thus becoming twenty seven; each was again modified by the three guс╣Зas, thus becoming eighty-one; the scene of their display extended to each of the ten regions of space, thus becoming the nine times ninety of the text, or 810

Jamison Brereton

With the bones of Dadhya├▒c unrepulsable Indra
smashed the nine and ninety obstacles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The use of the bones of Dadhya├▒c as a vajra-substitute is a particularly puzzling part of this puzzling version of the Dadhya├▒c myth. The appearance of this motif in the JB and MBh versions (see Geldner n. on vss. 13-15) seems to me an afterthe-fact rationalization of the verse here.

Griffith

With bones of Dadhyac for his arms, Indra, resistless in attack,
Struck nine-and-ninety Vrtras dead.

Geldner

Indra hat mit den Knochen des Dadhyanc unbehindert die neunmal neunzig Feinde erschlagen.

Grassmann

Mit Dadhiank’s Gebeinen schlug, Indra, dem niemand widersteht, Die neunundneunzig Feinde todt.

Elizarenkova

рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрд╖реБ рдкрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдореН рдЕрдкрдЧрддреНрдп рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рджрдзреАрдЪрдГ рдпрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рд░рдГ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╕рд░рд╕рд┐ рддрддреН рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рджрддреН рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реАрддреН ред рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрджрд╛рд╣реГрддреНрдп рддрджреАрдпреИрд░рд╕реНрдерд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЬрдШрд╛рдиреЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореГрдЪрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН ред рдЗрд╖реБ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН ’ ред рддреБрджрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╢рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рд╡рд┐рджрддреН ред рд╡реЗрддреНрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдЪреНрд▓реЗрдГ рдЕрдЩрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛ рдирд╛рдо рджреЗрд╢рд╛рдГред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдорджреВрд░рднрд╡рдВ рд╕рд░рдГ рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддреН ред рдордзреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН рдордзреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рек. реи.реорем) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрд╛рддреБрд░рд░реНрдерд┐рдХреЛ рдорддреБрдкреН ред’ рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреБрдкреЛ рд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН ред ‘рдорддреМ рдмрд╣реНрд╡рдЪреЛрд╜рдирдЬрд┐рд░рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдореН ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рей. резрезреп ) рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ рее

рднрдЯреНрдЯрднрд╛рд╕реНрдХрд░-рдЯреАрдХрд╛

2 рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ рее рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рдпрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рд░рдГ рд╢рд┐рд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрд╖реБ рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдореЗрдШреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рддрд┐рд░реЛрднреВрдп рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдВ рддрджрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рджрддреН рдЕрд▓рдмреНрдз ред рд▓реБрдЩреН ‘рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдЩреНрдпреЛрдЧреЗрд╜рдкрд┐’рдЗрддреНрдпрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ ред рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдореНрдирд┐ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ рд▓рдмреНрдзрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЙрдкрд▓рдмреНрдзрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдореВрд╣рд╡рджрдзрд┐рддреНрдпрдХрд╛рд╡рджрд┐рддрд┐ рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рддреН ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд░реНрдордгреАрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЗ рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWishing for the horse’s head hidden in the mountains, he found is ┼Ъaryaс╣З─Бvat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The head of the horse that he was seeking set away in the mountains, that he found in the reed-filled (lake?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntax of this verse is somewhat unclear. I take ab as a rel. clause with the pres. part. ich├бn functioning as the main verb and an unusual, indeed disturbing, position of the rel. pron. y├бd (we might expect *ich├бn y├бd ├б┼Ыvasya тАж), which is then picked up by t├бd in the main clause of c. Most other tr. take ich├бn as part of the main clause and the y├бd as the marker of an embedded rel. cl.: roughly тАЬseeking the head of the horse, which was set away in the mountains, he found itтАжтАЭ But not only would I prefer not to allow embedded relatives in the RV, but the position of y├бd makes this interpretation difficult, too (expect *ich├бnn ├б┼Ыvasya ┼Ы├нraс╕е y├бd тАж?).

Griffith

He, searching for the horse’s head, removed among the mountains, found
At Saryanavan what he sought.

Geldner

Als er den Kopf des Pferdes, der im Gebirg versteckt war, suchte, fand er ihn in Saryanavat.

Grassmann

Verlangend nach des Rosses Haupt, das in den Bergen sich versteckt, Fand er’s am somareichen Ort.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпрдереЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдпрдЪреНрдЫрд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рдкрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рд╢рд┐рд░реЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрдЬреНрдЬрдШрд╛рди рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдпрд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдВ рдЫреЗрддреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рджрд▓реНрд▓рднреЗрддреН рее резрек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп) рдЖрд╢реБрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ (рдпрддреН) (рд╢рд┐рд░рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдореН (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрд╖реБ) рд╢реИрд▓реЗрд╖реБ рдореЗрдШрд╛рд╡рдпрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрдкрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдореН) рдЖрд╕реЗрд╡рд┐рддрдореН (рддрддреН) (рд╡рд┐рджрддреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рддреН (рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгрд╛рд╡рддрд┐) рд╢рд░реНрдпрдгреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рджреЗрд╢рд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреВрд░рднрд╡реЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪред (рдЕрежред рек.реи.реорей) рдЕрдиреЗрди рдорддреБрдкреН рее резрек рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдореЗрдШрдВ рдЫрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рднреВрдореМ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрдпрддрд┐, рддрдереИрд╡ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрджреБрд░реНрдЧрд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдордкрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдВ рд╣рддреНрд╡рд╛ рднреВрдореМ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрдпреЗрддреН рдиреИрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рд╛ рднрд╡рд┐рддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдпрд╛ рее резрек рее

3 рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ рее рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрдГ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдЧреЛрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реБрдореНрдирд╛ рдЦреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдпрддреН рдирд╛рдо рдирдордирдВ рдЬрдЧрджреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣реНрд╡реАрднрд╛рд╡рдГ рдЕрдкреАрдЪреНрдпрдВ рдкреБрдирд░рдЮреНрдЪрд┐рддрдВ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрджреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрдВ рдЕрддреНрд░ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдЕрдордиреНрд╡рдд рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╡рдиреНрдд: рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреЗрди рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рд╣реЗрддреБрдирд╛ рд╕ рддрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕реЛрдкрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдЗрддреНрдерд╛ рдЗрддреНрдердореЗрд╡ рдЧреЛрд░реНрдирд╛рдо рдордиреНрд╡рддреЗ рдЕрдиреЗрди рд╣реЗрддреБрдиреЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдерд╛рд╣реЗрддреМ рдЪ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдерд╛рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рее

‘рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣ рдЧреМрд░рдордиреНрд╡рддреЗрддрд┐’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. реи. рем.),

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe (solar rays) found on this occasion the light of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б verily concealed in the mansion of the moving moon.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The text has only ’they found’; ─Аditya-ra┼Ыmayaс╕е, rays of the sun is added. Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б = the Sun, an ─Аditya; also, identified with Indra, to whom the hymn is addressed. ‘The rays of the sun are reflected back in the bright watery orb of the moon’; ’the solar radiance, concealed by the night, enters into the moon, and thus dispels darkness by night, as well as by day’. One ray of the sun (that named ┼Ыuс╣гumn─Б lights up the moon; therefore, moon’s light is derived from the sun (Nirukta 2,6)(cf. Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa 36)

Jamison Brereton

Right there they thought of the secret name of the cow of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАФ likewise in the house of the moon.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I confess myself to be entirely baffled by this verse, though the grammar is straightforward. GeldnerтАЩs reconstruction of the mythology (n. to vs. 15) is not entirely compelling, nor is that found in Witzel Got┼Н.

Griffith

Then verily they recognized the essential form of Tvastar’s Bull,
Here in the mansion of the Moon.

Geldner

Da erinnerten sie sich an den geheimen Namen der Kuh des Tvastri daselbst im Hause des Mondes

Grassmann

Dort fanden sie das Wesen auf des Stiers, den Tvaschtar hielt versteckt. Dort endlich in des Mondes Haus.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдЮреНрдЬрдЧрддрд┐ (рдЕрд╣) рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣реЗ (рдЧреЛрдГ) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдордиреНрд╡рдд) рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ (рдирд╛рдо) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рд░рдЪрдирдВ рдирд╛рдордХрд░рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрдГ) рдореВрд░реНрддрджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдЫреЗрджрдХрд╕реНрдп (рдЕрдкреАрдЪреНрдпрдореН) рдпреЗрд╜рдкреНрдпрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдореН (рдЗрддреНрдерд╛) рдЕрдиреЗрди рд╣реЗрддреБрдирд╛ (рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕рдГ) рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рджреЗрдГ (рдЧреГрд╣реЗ) рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рее резрел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho yokes todya to the pole of the car (of Indra) his vigorous and radiant steeds, whose fury is unbearable, in whose mouths are arrows, who trample on the hearts (of enemies), who give happiness (to friends). (The sacrificer) who praises their (performance of their) duties obtains (long) life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who today yokes the cattle to the chariot-pole of truthтАФthe vehement, wrathful, very angry ones,
with arrows in their mouths, shooting at the heart, but embodying joy? Whoever will succeed in bringing them, he will live.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The consensus of modern tr. is that the objects that the subject is struggling to yoke are the priests (see esp. Geldner), but I find this unlikely. The violent adjectival descriptors seem uncharacteristic for priests, but quite suitable for the Maruts, to whom the poet of this hymn (now drawing to a close) will dedicate the next four hymns. Note esp. that both ┼Ы├нmivant- and mayobh┼л╠Б- are used of the Maruts, once in the same hymn (VIII.20.3 and 24 respectively; for mayobh┼л╠Б- see also I.166.3, V.58.2). I therefore take the Maruts as referents of the acc. pls. and also suggest that this verse is the pivot for the Marut reference found also (in my interpretation) in vss.

10-12. In that tс╣Ыca the Maruts are referred to in the guise of clearly feminine bovine figures; here the cattle (g─Б╠Бс╕е) are the first acc. object we encounter. Because g├│- has fluctuating gender, this form can of course be feminine (as the bovines were in 10- 12), but the immediate following adjectives establish it decisively as masculine. If both 10-12 and this verse refer to the Maruts, this verse returns them to their proper grammatical gender. L├╝ders (Varuс╣Зa II.455) also thinks the Maruts are the referents.

с╣Ыt├бsya can be construed with either dhur├н or g─Б╠Бс╕е, and tr. divide on which they choose. I attach it to the chariot pole in part because с╣Ыt├бsya is often construed with a place (e.g., frequent с╣Ыt├бsya y├│ni-), but the other is not impossible: cf. I.73.6 r╠еt├бsya … dhen├бvaс╕е.

Griffith

Who yokes to-day unto the pole of Order the strong and passionate steers of checkless spirit,
With shaft-armed mouths, heart-piercing, health-bestowing?
Long shall he live who richly pays their service.

Geldner

Wer schirrt heute die Rinder an das Joch der Opferordnung, die heftigen grimmigen, ungn├дdigen, die Pfeile im Munde f├╝hren, die ins Herz treffen und doch heilsam sind? Wem ihre Pflege gl├╝ckt, der soll leben.

Grassmann

Wer schirrt ans Joch des Opfers heut die Stiere, die kr├дftig sind, voll regen Eifers, strahlend, Im Munde Pfeile, herzverwundend, labend? Wer recht sie pflegt, der muss am Leben bleiben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho goes forth, (through dread of foes, when Indra is at hand); who is harmed (by his enemies); who is terrified; who is aware that Indra is present, who that he is night? What need is there that any one should importune Indra for his son, his elephant, his property, his person n, or his people?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kaс╕е = praj─Бpati

Jamison Brereton

Who retreats and who is thrust back? Who is fearful? Who might think Indra exists? Who (might think he is) nearby?
Who will speak for offspring, who for a retinue and for wealth? Who will speak on behalf of himself, on behalf of his people?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Contra the interpretation of ├нbha- as тАШelephantтАЩ in Vedic (so Geldner), see EWA s.v. _________ 18
yaj─Бtai is, as far as I can tell, the only RVic examples of a medial 3rd sg.

subjunctive in -tai, the form that takes over beginning with the AV, spreading from the 1st sg. As such it may be a sign that at least this part of this last hymn in the Indra group is late.

P─Бda c presents a problem that has been glossed over by most modern tr.: the active of ─Б╠БтИЪvah should take an acc. of what is being conveyed, but it is distinctly odd to say that the gods are bringing the oblation here. Geldner (Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) avoid the difficulty by interpreting the verb as intrans. тАШfahrenтАЩ (/тАШarriver-en-charтАЩ), a usage associated with the middle, with h├│ma an acc. of goal. Oldenberg, however, disapproves of this makeshift (as do I), setting out the arguments very clearly. Though he agrees that тАЬder Gedanke befremdet,тАЭ he sticks to the expected syntax (as do I) and cites a number of passages in which gods do bring oblations. The closest is V.41.7 in which Night and Dawn bring the sacrifice to the mortal (V.41.7d ─Б╠Бh─Б vahato m├бrty─Бya yaj├▒├бm). I suggest that the role-switch in this verse (gods bring the oblation, rather than coming to our oblation to take it away) is also found in the next verse, where the god praises the mortal.

Griffith

Who fleeth forth? who suffereth? who feareth? Who knoweth Indra present, Indra near us?
Who sendeth benediction on his offspring, his household, wealth and person, and the People?

Elizarenkova

рдЗрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореНрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho praises the (sacrificial) fire, (lighted for Indra), or worships him with the oblation of clarified butter, presented in the ladle, according to the constant seasons? To whom do the gods quickly bring (the wealth) that has been called for? What sacrificer, engaged in offering oblations and favoured by the gods, thoroughly knows Indra?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъtubhir dhruvebhiс╕е, according to the constant seasons; alternative reading: ‘presented by the divinities called с╣Ъtus, who preside over sacrifices’ (e.g., с╣Ыtavo vai pray─Бj─Бс╕е, the с╣Ыtus are the chief sacrifices, i.e. pray─Бj─Бdevat─Бс╕е, the deities presiding over the sacrifices).

Jamison Brereton

Who reverently invokes Agni with oblation and ghee? (Who)
will perform sacrifice with a ladle according to the fixed ritual
sequences?
For whom will the gods swiftly convey the offering here? Who might think himself a man whose oblations are worth pursuing, who has
gods well on his side?

Griffith

Who with poured oil and offering honours Agni, with ladle worships at appointed seasons?
To whom to the Gods bring oblation quickly? What offerer, God-favoured, knows him thoroughly?

Geldner

Wer ruft den Agni mit Schmalzopfer an und will mit dem L├╢ffel zu den bestimmten Zeiten opfern? F├╝r wen werden die G├╢tter rasch zu dem Opfer fahren? Wer, der das Hotri-Amt besorgt, darf sich f├╝r einen G├╢tterliebling halten?

Grassmann

Wer ehrt mit fettem Opferguss den Agni, mit L├╢ffeln opfernd zu den festen Zeiten? Wem f├╝hren starke Tr├дnke zu die G├╢tter? wer gilt den G├╢ttern lieb zum Mahl sie ladend?

English translation:

тАЬPowerful, Indra, be present and be favourable to the mortal (who adores you); there is no other giver of felicity, Maghavan, than you; hence, Indra, I recite your praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Surely you, (though) a god, will solemnly praise the mortal, o
strongest one.
There is no other dispenser of mercy than you, bounteous one. Indra, I say this speech to you:

Jamison Brereton Notes

As in the last verse the usual ritual roles of god and mortal are reversed, with Indra producing a pra┼Ыasti of a mortal. I do not understand why, but, unlike 18c, there is no way to wriggle out of the undeniable purport of this verb phrase - thus supporting the тАЬgods convey the oblationтАЭ interpretation of 18c.

tv├бm aс╣Еg├б reprises the tag of vss. 7-9, ├нndro aс╣Еg├б, with of course the same referent.

I follow Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) in taking vs. 20 as the quoted v├бcaс╕е of p─Бda d, though it would be equally possible to interpret v├бcaс╕е as referring to what precedes, indeed even to the whole of the hymn.

Thou as a God, O Mightiest, verily blessest mortal man.
O Maghavan, there is no comforter but thou: Indra, I speak my words to thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGranter of dwellings, let not your treasury, let not your benefits, ever be detrimental to us. Friend of mankind, bring to us, who are acquainted with prayers, all sorts of riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Benefits: ┼лtayaс╕е, benefits, assistances; also, dh┼лtayaс╕е, shakers, agitators, i.e. the Maruts or winds

Jamison Brereton

Let not your benefits, nor your help, good one, ever cheat us.
And mete out to us all goods coming from the settled domains, you who belong to the descendants of Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is tempting to take dabhan as related to or contextually assimilated to dabhr├б- тАШpaltry, fewтАЩ in the meaning тАШcome up shortтАЩ, though the asm─Б╠Бn would be more difficult to construe.

Griffith

Let not thy bounteous gifts, let not thy saving help fail us, good Lord, at any time;
And measure out to us, thou lover of mankind, all riches hitherward from men.

Geldner

Nicht sollen uns deine Gaben, nicht deine Hilfen jemals t├дuschen, du Guter. Und weise uns von allen V├╢lkern alle G├╝ter zu, du Menschenfreund!

Grassmann

Nie m├╢gen deine Gaben, deine H├╝lfen nie im Stich uns lassen, g├╝tiger! Und alle G├╝ter miss, o menschenfreundlicher, uns und der ganzen Menschheit zu.

Elizarenkova

(рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ (рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рдзрди (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рд╣рдордХреЛ (рдХрджрд╛рдЪрди) рдХрднреА рднреА (рдорд╛ рджрднрдиреН) рджреБрдГрдЦрджрд╛рдпрдХ рди рд╣реЛрдВ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реА (рдКрддрдпрдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рд╣рдордХреЛ (рдорд╛) рдордд рджреБрдГрдЦрджрд╛рдпреА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗред рд╣реЗ (рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрдд ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рддреВ (рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгрд┐рднреНрдпрдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗ (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреЗрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣рдордХреЛ рднреА рджреЗ (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдордХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреА (рдЖ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ (рдЙрдкрдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐) рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░ рее реиреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рдЬрд┐рдирдХрд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░, рдорди рдФрд░ рдзрди рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░реЗ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рдЬреЛ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЗ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее реиреж рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг-рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рдВрдЧ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╕реЛ ! рддреЗ рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдВрд╕реНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдХрджрд╛рдЪрди рдорд╛ рджрднрдиреНред рдд рдКрддрдпреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддреБред рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖ ! рдпрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгрд┐рднреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рджрджрд╛рд╕рд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЙрдкрдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐ рее реиреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рддреЗ) (рд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдорд╛) (рддреЗ) (рдКрддрдпрдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╡рд╕реЛ) рд╕реБрдЦреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддрдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН) (рдХрджрд╛) (рдЪрди) рдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ (рджрднрдиреН) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрдпреБрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЪ) рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЙрдкрдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдареИрд░реБрдкрдорд┐рддрд╛рдиреН рдХреБрд░реБ (рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгрд┐рднреНрдпрдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдореЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ (рдЖ) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рее реиреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдд рдПрд╡ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХрд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддрдиреБрд░реНрдордиреЛ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЦрдпреЗрдпреБрдГред рдд рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЗ рдЪ рдЬрдЧрджреБрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рее реиреж рее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рддреАрдЪ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд╢рд░реАрд░, рдорди, рдзрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗрддреЗ рддреАрдЪ рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рдЬреА рдЬрдЧрд╛рд╡рд░ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд.
